class="infobox-data">(+46) 31</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data">\n<ul><li><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external Short ENG description</a></span></li>\n<li><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://international.goteborg.se">international<wbr />.goteborg<wbr />.se</a></span></li></ul>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Gothenburg</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="/\xc9\xa1/: &#39;g&#39; in &#39;guy&#39;">\xc9\xa1</span><span title="/\xc9\x92/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;body&#39;">\xc9\x92</span><span title="/\xce\xb8/: &#39;th&#39; in &#39;thigh&#39;">\xce\xb8</span><span title="/\xc9\x99n/: &#39;on&#39; in &#39;button&#39;">\xc9\x99n</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/\xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r/: &#39;ur&#39; in &#39;fur&#39;">\xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r</span><span title="/\xc9\xa1/: &#39;g&#39; in &#39;guy&#39;">\xc9\xa1</span></span>/</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-Gothenburg.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/23/En-Gothenburg.ogg" class="internal" title="En-Gothenburg.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> abbreviated <b>Gbg</b>;<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>: <i lang="sv">G\xc3\xb6teborg</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Swedish" title="Help:IPA/Swedish">[j\xc5\x93t\xc9\x9b\xcb\x88b\xc9\x94rj]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sv-G%C3%B6teborg.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/10/Sv-G%C3%B6teborg.ogg" class="internal" title="Sv-G\xc3\xb6teborg.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>) is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_in_Sweden_by_population" title="List of urban areas in Sweden by population">second-largest city</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, fifth-largest in the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic countries</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">capital</a> of the <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A4stra_G%C3%B6taland_County" title="V\xc3\xa4stra G\xc3\xb6taland County">V\xc3\xa4stra G\xc3\xb6taland County</a>. It is situated by <a href="/wiki/Kattegat" title="Kattegat">Kattegat</a>, on the west coast of Sweden, and has a population of approximately 570,000 in the <a href="/wiki/City_proper" title="City proper">city proper</a> and about 1 million inhabitants in the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Gothenburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Metropolitan Gothenburg">metropolitan area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-scb_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scb-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gothenburg was founded as a heavily fortified, primarily Dutch, trading colony, by <a href="/wiki/Royal_charter" title="Royal charter">royal charter</a> in 1621 by <a href="/wiki/King_Gustavus_Adolphus" class="mw-redirect" title="King Gustavus Adolphus">King Gustavus Adolphus</a>. In addition to the generous privileges (e.g. tax relaxation) given to his Dutch allies from the then-ongoing <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years&#39; War">Thirty Years\' War</a>, the king also attracted significant numbers of his <a href="/wiki/German_people" class="mw-redirect" title="German people">German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_people" title="Scottish people">Scottish</a> allies to populate his only town on the western coast. At a key strategic location at the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6ta_%C3%A4lv" title="G\xc3\xb6ta \xc3\xa4lv">G\xc3\xb6ta \xc3\xa4lv</a>, where Scandinavia\'s largest drainage basin enters the sea, the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Gothenburg" title="Port of Gothenburg">Port of Gothenburg</a> is now the largest port in the Nordic countries.<sup id="cite_ref-selimw_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-selimw-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gothenburg is home to many students, as the city includes the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Gothenburg" title="University of Gothenburg">University of Gothenburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chalmers_University_of_Technology" title="Chalmers University of Technology">Chalmers University of Technology</a>. <a href="/wiki/Volvo" title="Volvo">Volvo</a> was founded in Gothenburg in 1927.<sup id="cite_ref-volvo-founders_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-volvo-founders-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The original parent Volvo Group and the now separate <a href="/wiki/Volvo_Car_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Volvo Car Corporation">Volvo Car Corporation</a> are still headquartered on the island of <a href="/wiki/Hisingen" title="Hisingen">Hisingen</a> in the city. Other key companies are <a href="/wiki/SKF" title="SKF">SKF</a> and <a href="/wiki/AstraZeneca" title="AstraZeneca">AstraZeneca</a>.\n</p><p>Gothenburg is served by <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6teborg_Landvetter_Airport" title="G\xc3\xb6teborg Landvetter Airport">G\xc3\xb6teborg Landvetter Airport</a> 30&#160;km (19&#160;mi) southeast of the city center. The smaller <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6teborg_City_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="G\xc3\xb6teborg City Airport">G\xc3\xb6teborg City Airport</a>, 15&#160;km (9.3&#160;mi) from the city center, was closed to regular airline traffic in 2015.\n</p><p>The city hosts the <a href="/wiki/Gothia_Cup" title="Gothia Cup">Gothia Cup</a>, the world\'s largest youth football tournament, and the <a href="https://sv.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%B6teborg_Basketball_Festival" class="extiw" title="sv:G\xc3\xb6teborg Basketball Festival">G\xc3\xb6teborg Basketball Festival</a>, Europe\'s largest youth basketball tournament, alongside some of the largest annual events in Scandinavia. The <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_Film_Festival" title="Gothenburg Film Festival">Gothenburg Film Festival</a>, held in January since 1979, is the leading Scandinavian film festival with over 155,000 visitors each year.<sup id="cite_ref-filmfestival_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-filmfestival-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In summer, a wide variety of music festivals are held in the city, including the popular <a href="/wiki/Way_Out_West_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Way Out West Festival">Way Out West Festival</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#References"><span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Name_of_the_Goths" title="Name of the Goths">Name of the Goths</a></div>\n<p>The city was named G\xc3\xb6teborg in the city\'s charter in 1621<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and simultaneously given the German and English name Gothenburg.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The Swedish name was given after the <i>G\xc3\xb6ta \xc3\xa4lv</i>, called <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6ta_River" class="mw-redirect" title="G\xc3\xb6ta River">G\xc3\xb6ta River</a> in English,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and other cities ending in <i>-borg</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Both the Swedish and German/English names were in use before 1621 and had already been used for the previous city founded in 1604 that burned down in 1611.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Gothenburg is one of few Swedish cities to still have an official and widely used <a href="/wiki/Exonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Exonym">exonym</a>.\n</p><p>The city council of 1641 consisted of four Swedish, three Dutch, three German, and two Scottish members. In <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a>, English, and German, all languages with a long history in this trade and maritime-oriented city, the name Gothenburg is or was (in the case of German) used for the city. Variations of the official German/English name Gothenburg in the city\'s 1621 charter existed or exist in many languages. The French form of the city name is <i>Gothembourg</i>, but in French texts, the Swedish name <i>G\xc3\xb6teborg</i> is more frequent. "Gothenburg" can also be seen in some older English texts. In Spanish and Portuguese the city is called Gotemburgo. These traditional forms are sometimes replaced with the use of the Swedish <i>G\xc3\xb6teborg</i>, for example by <a href="/wiki/The_G%C3%B6teborg_Opera" class="mw-redirect" title="The G\xc3\xb6teborg Opera">The G\xc3\xb6teborg Opera</a> and the G\xc3\xb6teborg Ballet. However, <i>G\xc3\xb6teborgs universitet</i>, previously designated as the G\xc3\xb6teborg University in English, changed its name to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Gothenburg" title="University of Gothenburg">University of Gothenburg</a> in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The Gothenburg municipality has also reverted to the use of the English name in international contexts.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2009, the city council launched a new logotype for Gothenburg. Since the name "G\xc3\xb6teborg" contains the Swedish letter "\xc3\xb6", they planned to make the name more international and "up to date" by turning the "\xc3\xb6" sideways. As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the name is spelled "Go:teborg" on a large number of signs in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Gothenburg" title="History of Gothenburg">History of Gothenburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Gothenburg" title="Timeline of Gothenburg">Timeline of Gothenburg</a></div>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_Europe" title="Early modern Europe">early modern period</a>, the configuration of Sweden\'s borders made Gothenburg strategically critical as the only Swedish gateway to <a href="/wiki/Skagerrak" title="Skagerrak">Skagerrak</a>, the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a>, situated on the west coast in a very narrow strip of Swedish territory between Danish <a href="/wiki/Halland" title="Halland">Halland</a> in the south and Norwegian <a href="/wiki/Bohusl%C3%A4n" title="Bohusl\xc3\xa4n">Bohusl\xc3\xa4n</a> in the north. After several failed attempts, Gothenburg was successfully founded in 1621 by <a href="/wiki/Gustavus_Adolphus_of_Sweden" title="Gustavus Adolphus of Sweden">King Gustavus Adolphus</a> (Gustaf&#160;II Adolf).<sup id="cite_ref-stad_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stad-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The site of the first church built in Gothenburg, subsequently destroyed by Danish invaders, is marked by a stone near the north end of the <a href="/wiki/%C3%84lvsborg_Bridge" title="\xc3\x84lvsborg Bridge">\xc3\x84lvsborg Bridge</a> in the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A4rjen%C3%A4sparken" title="F\xc3\xa4rjen\xc3\xa4sparken">F\xc3\xa4rjen\xc3\xa4s Park</a>. The church was built in 1603 and destroyed in 1611.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The city was heavily influenced by the Dutch, Germans, and Scots, and Dutch planners and engineers were contracted to construct the city as they had the skills needed to drain and build in the marshy areas chosen for the city. The town was designed like Dutch cities such as <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Batavia,_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Batavia, Dutch East Indies">Batavia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>) and <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">New Amsterdam</a> (<a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-stad_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stad-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The planning of the streets and canals of Gothenburg closely resembled that of Jakarta, which was built by the Dutch around the same time.<sup id="cite_ref-kastrup75_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kastrup75-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The Dutchmen initially won political power, and it was not until 1652, when the last Dutch politician in the city\'s council died, that Swedes acquired political power over Gothenburg.<sup id="cite_ref-REF88_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-REF88-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> During the Dutch period, the town followed Dutch town laws and Dutch was proposed as the official language in the town. Robust city walls were built during the 17th century. In 1807, a decision was made to tear down most of the city\'s wall. The work started in 1810 and was carried out by 150 soldiers from the Bohus regiment.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Along with the Dutch, the town also was heavily influenced by Scots who settled down in Gothenburg. Many became people of high-profile.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/William_Chalmers_(merchant)" title="William Chalmers (merchant)">William Chalmers</a>, the son of a Scottish immigrant, donated his fortunes to set up what later became the <a href="/wiki/Chalmers_University_of_Technology" title="Chalmers University of Technology">Chalmers University of Technology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In 1841, the Scotsman <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Keiller_(businessman)" title="Alexander Keiller (businessman)">Alexander Keiller</a> founded the <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6taverken" title="G\xc3\xb6taverken">G\xc3\xb6taverken</a> shipbuilding company that was in business until 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> His son James Keiller donated Keiller Park to the city in 1906.<sup id="cite_ref-Keiller_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keiller-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Gothenburg" title="Coat of arms of Gothenburg">Gothenburg coat of arms</a> was based on the lion of the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Sweden" title="Coat of arms of Sweden">coat of arms of Sweden</a>, symbolically holding a shield with the national emblem, the <a href="/wiki/Three_Crowns" title="Three Crowns">Three Crowns</a>, to defend the city against its enemies.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Roskilde" title="Treaty of Roskilde">Treaty of Roskilde</a> (1658), <a href="/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Norway" title="Denmark\xe2\x80\x93Norway">Denmark\xe2\x80\x93Norway</a> ceded the then Danish province Halland, in the south, and the Norwegian province of Bohus County or <i>Bohusl\xc3\xa4n</i> in the north, leaving Gothenburg less exposed. Gothenburg was able to grow into a significant port and trade centre on the west coast, because it was the only city on the west coast that, along with <a href="/wiki/Marstrand" title="Marstrand">Marstrand</a>, was granted the rights to trade with merchants from other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-REF88_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-REF88-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 18th century, fishing was the most important industry. However, in 1731, the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_East_India_Company" title="Swedish East India Company">Swedish East India Company</a> was founded, and the city flourished due to its foreign trade with highly profitable commercial expeditions to China.<sup id="cite_ref-Nordisk_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nordisk-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The harbour developed into Sweden\'s main harbour for trade towards the west, and when Swedish emigration to the United States increased, Gothenburg became Sweden\'s main point of departure for these travellers. The impact of Gothenburg as a main port of embarkation for Swedish emigrants is reflected by <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg,_Nebraska" title="Gothenburg, Nebraska">Gothenburg, Nebraska</a>, a small Swedish settlement in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With the 19th century, Gothenburg evolved into a modern industrial city that continued on into the 20th century. The population increased tenfold in the century, from 13,000 (1800) to 130,000 (1900).<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>  In the 20th century, major companies that developed included <a href="/wiki/SKF" title="SKF">SKF</a> (1907)<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Volvo" title="Volvo">Volvo</a> (1927).<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1108px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:G%C3%B6teborg_Panorama.jpg" class="image" title="Panoramic view of Gothenburg&#39;s downtown coast line"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/G%C3%B6teborg_Panorama.jpg/1100px-G%C3%B6teborg_Panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="1100" height="199" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/G%C3%B6teborg_Panorama.jpg/1650px-G%C3%B6teborg_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/G%C3%B6teborg_Panorama.jpg/2200px-G%C3%B6teborg_Panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="15387" data-file-height="2778" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:G%C3%B6teborg_Panorama.jpg" title="File:G\xc3\xb6teborg Panorama.jpg"> </a></div>Panoramic view of Gothenburg\'s downtown coast line</div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:G%C3%B6teborg_in_moon_light.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/G%C3%B6teborg_in_moon_light.jpg/220px-G%C3%B6teborg_in_moon_light.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/G%C3%B6teborg_in_moon_light.jpg/330px-G%C3%B6teborg_in_moon_light.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/G%C3%B6teborg_in_moon_light.jpg/440px-G%C3%B6teborg_in_moon_light.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2016" data-file-height="1512" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:G%C3%B6teborg_in_moon_light.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View from \xc3\x84lvsborg Bridge</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gothenburg_bu_Sentinel-2,_2020-08-15.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Gothenburg_bu_Sentinel-2%2C_2020-08-15.jpg/220px-Gothenburg_bu_Sentinel-2%2C_2020-08-15.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Gothenburg_bu_Sentinel-2%2C_2020-08-15.jpg/330px-Gothenburg_bu_Sentinel-2%2C_2020-08-15.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Gothenburg_bu_Sentinel-2%2C_2020-08-15.jpg/440px-Gothenburg_bu_Sentinel-2%2C_2020-08-15.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3783" data-file-height="3536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gothenburg_bu_Sentinel-2,_2020-08-15.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Satellite picture of Gothenburg</div></div></div>\n<p>Gothenburg is located on the west coast, in southwestern Sweden, about halfway between the capitals <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, Denmark, and <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>, Norway. The location at the mouth of the G\xc3\xb6ta \xc3\xa4lv, which feeds into <a href="/wiki/Kattegat" title="Kattegat">Kattegatt</a>, an arm of the North Sea, has helped the city grow in significance as a <a href="/wiki/Trading_post" title="Trading post">trading city</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_archipelago" title="Gothenburg archipelago">archipelago of Gothenburg</a> consists of rough, barren rocks and cliffs, which also is typical for the coast of Bohusl\xc3\xa4n.<sup id="cite_ref-Uggle_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Uggle-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Due to the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>, the city has a mild climate and moderately heavy precipitation.<sup id="cite_ref-gulf_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gulf-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> It is the second-largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_Swedish_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Swedish cities">city in Sweden</a> after the capital <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Gothenburg Metropolitan Area (<i>Stor-G\xc3\xb6teborg</i>) has 982,360 inhabitants and extends to the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Ale_Municipality" title="Ale Municipality">Ale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alings%C3%A5s" title="Alings\xc3\xa5s">Alings\xc3\xa5s</a>, G\xc3\xb6teborg, <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A4rryda" title="H\xc3\xa4rryda">H\xc3\xa4rryda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kung%C3%A4lv" title="Kung\xc3\xa4lv">Kung\xc3\xa4lv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lerum" title="Lerum">Lerum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lilla_Edet" title="Lilla Edet">Lilla Edet</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6lndal" title="M\xc3\xb6lndal">M\xc3\xb6lndal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Partille" title="Partille">Partille</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stenungsund" title="Stenungsund">Stenungsund</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tj%C3%B6rn" title="Tj\xc3\xb6rn">Tj\xc3\xb6rn</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%96cker%C3%B6" title="\xc3\x96cker\xc3\xb6">\xc3\x96cker\xc3\xb6</a> within <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A4stra_G%C3%B6taland_County" title="V\xc3\xa4stra G\xc3\xb6taland County">V\xc3\xa4stra G\xc3\xb6taland County</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kungsbacka" title="Kungsbacka">Kungsbacka</a> within <a href="/wiki/Halland_County" title="Halland County">Halland County</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Angered" title="Angered">Angered</a>, a suburb outside Gothenburg, consists of Hj\xc3\xa4llbo, Eriksbo, Rannebergen, Hammarkullen, G\xc3\xa5rdsten, and L\xc3\xb6vg\xc3\xa4rdet.<sup id="cite_ref-gatunamn_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gatunamn-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> It is a <a href="/wiki/Million_Programme" title="Million Programme">Million Programme</a> part of Gothenburg, like <a href="/wiki/Roseng%C3%A5rd" title="Roseng\xc3\xa5rd">Roseng\xc3\xa5rd</a> in Malm\xc3\xb6 and <a href="/wiki/Botkyrka_Municipality" title="Botkyrka Municipality">Botkyrka</a> in Stockholm.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Angered had about 50,000 inhabitants in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup>[?]</sup> It lies north of Gothenburg and is isolated from the rest of the city. <a href="/wiki/Bergsj%C3%B6n" title="Bergsj\xc3\xb6n">Bergsj\xc3\xb6n</a> is another Million Programme suburb north of Gothenburg, it has 14,000 inhabitants. Biskopsg\xc3\xa5rden is the biggest multicultural suburb on the island of <a href="/wiki/Hisingen" title="Hisingen">Hisingen</a>, which is a part of Gothenburg but separated from the city by the river.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:2008px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Gothenburg-Panorama-20110911.jpg" class="image" title="A panorama of central Gothenburg taken from Keillers park, facing south \xe2\x80\x93 from left to right: G\xc3\xb6ta \xc3\xa4lvbron, Lilla Bommen, Viking, The G\xc3\xb6teborg Opera in front of G\xc3\xb6teborgshjulet, Skansen Kronan, Oscar Fredrik Church, Masthugg Church, and \xc3\x84lvsborg Bridge"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Gothenburg-Panorama-20110911.jpg/2000px-Gothenburg-Panorama-20110911.jpg" decoding="async" width="2000" height="168" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Gothenburg-Panorama-20110911.jpg/3000px-Gothenburg-Panorama-20110911.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Gothenburg-Panorama-20110911.jpg/4000px-Gothenburg-Panorama-20110911.jpg 2x" data-file-width="14318" data-file-height="1200" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gothenburg-Panorama-20110911.jpg" title="File:Gothenburg-Panorama-20110911.jpg"> </a></div>A panorama of central Gothenburg taken from Keillers park, facing south \xe2\x80\x93 from left to right: <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6ta_%C3%A4lvbron" class="mw-redirect" title="G\xc3\xb6ta \xc3\xa4lvbron">G\xc3\xb6ta \xc3\xa4lvbron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lilla_Bommen" title="Lilla Bommen">Lilla Bommen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viking_(barque)" title="Viking (barque)">Viking</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_G%C3%B6teborg_Opera" class="mw-redirect" title="The G\xc3\xb6teborg Opera">The G\xc3\xb6teborg Opera</a> in front of <a href="/w/index.php?title=G%C3%B6teborgshjulet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="G\xc3\xb6teborgshjulet (page does not exist)">G\xc3\xb6teborgshjulet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skansen_Kronan" title="Skansen Kronan">Skansen Kronan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Fredrik_Church" title="Oscar Fredrik Church">Oscar Fredrik Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Masthugg_Church" title="Masthugg Church">Masthugg Church</a>, and <a href="/wiki/%C3%84lvsborg_Bridge" title="\xc3\x84lvsborg Bridge">\xc3\x84lvsborg Bridge</a></div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Gothenburg has an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic" class="mw-disambig" title="Oceanic">oceanic</a> climate according to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification</a>. Despite its northerly latitude, temperatures are quite mild throughout the year and warmer than places at a similar latitude like <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>, this is mainly because of the moderating influence of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gulf_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gulf-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> During the summer, daylight extends 18 hours and 5 minutes, but lasts 6 hours and 32 minutes in late December. The climate has become significantly milder in later decades, particularly in summer and winter; July temperatures used to be below Stockholm\'s 1961\xe2\x80\x931990 averages, but have since been warmer than that benchmark.\n</p><p>Summers are warm and pleasant with average high temperatures of 20 to 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (68 to 72&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and lows of 12 to 15&#160;\xc2\xb0C (54 to 59&#160;\xc2\xb0F), but temperatures of 25\xe2\x80\x9330&#160;\xc2\xb0C (77\xe2\x80\x9386&#160;\xc2\xb0F) occur on many days during the summer.\nWinters are cold and windy with temperatures of around \xe2\x88\x921 to 4&#160;\xc2\xb0C (30 to 39&#160;\xc2\xb0F), though it rarely drops below \xe2\x88\x9220&#160;\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x924&#160;\xc2\xb0F). Precipitation is regular but generally moderate throughout the year. Snow mainly occurs from December to March, but is not unusual in November and April and can sometimes occur even in October and May.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible" style="width:100%; text-align:center; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th Gothenburg\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Month\n</th>\n<th>Jan\n</th>\n<th>Feb\n</th>\n<th>Mar\n</th>\n<th>Apr\n</th>\n<th>May\n</th>\n<th>Jun\n</th>\n<th>Jul\n</th>\n<th>Aug\n</th>\n<th>Sep\n</th>\n<th>Oct\n</th>\n<th>Nov\n</th>\n<th>Dec\n</th>\n<th style="background:#f85900;color:#000000;">6\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f7e400;color:#000000;">5\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f7e400;color:#000000;">4\n</td>\n<td style="background:#289500;color:#000000;">2\n</td>\n<td style="background:#289500;color:#000000;">1\n</td>\n<td style="background:#289500;color:#000000;">0\n</td>\n<td style="background:#f7e400;color:#000000;border-left-width:medium">3\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="14" style="background:#f8f9fa;font-weight:normal;font-size:95%;">Source: Weather Atlas<sup
