data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_nature">Parks and nature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Parks and nature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BotDSCF3134.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/BotDSCF3134.jpg/220px-BotDSCF3134.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/BotDSCF3134.jpg/330px-BotDSCF3134.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/BotDSCF3134.jpg/440px-BotDSCF3134.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3488" data-file-height="2616" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BotDSCF3134.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Gothenburg Botanical Garden</div></div></div>\n<p>Gothenburg has several parks and <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserve" title="Nature reserve">nature reserves</a> ranging in size from tens of square metres to hundreds of hectares. It also has many green areas that are not designated as parks or reserves.\n</p><p>Selection of parks:\n</p>\n<ul><li><i>Kungsparken</i>, 13&#160;ha (32 acres), built between 1839 and 1861, surrounds the canal that circles the city centre.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Garden_Society_of_Gothenburg" title="Garden Society of Gothenburg">Garden Society of Gothenburg</a>, a park and horticultural garden, is located next to <a href="/wiki/Kungsportsavenyen" title="Kungsportsavenyen">Kungsportsavenyen</a>. Founded in 1842 by the Swedish king Carl XIV Johan and on initiative of the amateur botanist Henric Elof von Normann, the park has a noted rose garden with some 4,000 roses of 1,900 cultivars.<sup id="cite_ref-parker_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parker-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Slottsskogen" title="Slottsskogen">Slottsskogen</a>,  137&#160;ha (340 acres), was created in 1874 by August Kobb. It has a free "open" zoo that includes <a href="/wiki/Harbor_seal" title="Harbor seal">harbor seals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Penguin" title="Penguin">penguins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horse" title="Horse">horses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pig" title="Pig">pigs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moose" title="Moose">moose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goat" title="Goat">goats</a>, and many <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">birds</a>. The Natural History Museum (<i>Naturhistoriska Museet</i>) and the city\'s oldest observatory are located in the park.<sup id="cite_ref-parker_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parker-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The annual Way Out West festival is held in the park.<sup id="cite_ref-wow_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wow-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><i>\xc3\x84ngg\xc3\xa5rdsbergens naturreservat</i>, 320&#160;ha (790 acres), was bought in 1840 by pharmacist Arvid Gren, and donated in 1963 to the city by Sven and Carl Gren Broberg, who stated the area must remain a nature and <a href="/wiki/Bird_reserve" title="Bird reserve">bird reserve</a>. It lies partly in M\xc3\xb6lndal.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><i>Delsj\xc3\xb6omr\xc3\xa5dets naturreservat</i>, about 760&#160;ha (1,900 acres),<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> has been in use since the 17th century as a farming area; significant forest management was carried out in the late 19th century. Skat\xc3\xa5s gym and motionscentrum is situated here.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rya_skog" title="Rya skog">Rya Skogs Naturreservat</a>, 17&#160;ha (42 acres), became a protected area in 1928. It contains remnants of a defensive wall built in the mid- to late-17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><i>Keillers park</i> was donated by James Keiller in 1906. He was the son of Scottish Alexander Keiller, who founded the <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6taverken" title="G\xc3\xb6taverken">G\xc3\xb6taverken</a> shipbuilding company.<sup id="cite_ref-Keiller_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keiller-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gatunamn_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gatunamn-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><i>S A Hedlunds park</i>: <a href="/wiki/Sven_Adolf_Hedlund" title="Sven Adolf Hedlund">Sven Adolf Hedlund</a>, newspaper publisher and politician, bought the 15&#160;ha (37 acres) Bjursl\xc3\xa4tt farm in 1857, and in 1928 it was given to the city.</li>\n<li><i>Hisingsparken</i> is Gothenburg\'s largest park.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><i>Fluns\xc3\xa5sparken</i>, built in 1950, has many free activities during the summer such as concerts and theatre.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_Botanical_Garden" title="Gothenburg Botanical Garden">Gothenburg Botanical Garden</a>, 175&#160;ha (430 acres), opened in 1923.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> It won an award in 2003, and in 2006 was third in "The most beautiful garden in Europe" competition. It has around 16,000 species of plants and trees. The greenhouses contain around 4,500 species including 1,600 orchids.<sup id="cite_ref-parker_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parker-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> It is considered to be one of the most important <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical gardens</a> in Europe with three stars in the French <i>Guide Rouge</i>.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gothenburgcity.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Gothenburgcity.jpg/220px-Gothenburgcity.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Gothenburgcity.jpg/330px-Gothenburgcity.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Gothenburgcity.jpg/440px-Gothenburgcity.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gothenburgcity.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Many buildings in the old part of the city were built along canals.</div></div></div>\n<p>Very few houses are left from the 17th century when the city was founded, since all but the military and royal houses were built of wood.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> A rare exception is the <a href="/wiki/Skansen_Kronan" title="Skansen Kronan">Skansen Kronan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first major architecturally interesting period is the 18th century when the East India Company made Gothenburg an important trade city. Imposing stone houses in <a href="/wiki/Neo-Classical_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-Classical architecture">Neo-Classical</a> style were erected around the canals. One example from this period is the East India House, which today houses the <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6teborg_City_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="G\xc3\xb6teborg City Museum">G\xc3\xb6teborg City Museum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-capture_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-capture-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 19th century, the wealthy bourgeoisie began to move outside the city walls which had protected the city. The style now was an eclectic, academic, somewhat overdecorated style which the middle-class favoured. The working class lived in the overcrowded city district <a href="/wiki/Haga,_Gothenburg" title="Haga, Gothenburg">Haga</a> in wooden houses.<sup id="cite_ref-varde_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-varde-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 19th century, the first comprehensive town plan after the founding of city was created, which led to the construction of the main street, Kungsportsavenyen.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Perhaps the most significant type of houses of the city, <a href="/wiki/Landsh%C3%B6vdingehus" title="Landsh\xc3\xb6vdingehus">Landsh\xc3\xb6vdingehusen</a>, were built in the end of the 19th century \xe2\x80\x93 three-storey houses with the first floor in stone and the other two in wood.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The early 20th century, characterized by the <a href="/wiki/Romantic_nationalism" title="Romantic nationalism">National Romantic</a> style, was rich in architectural achievements.<sup id="cite_ref-varde_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-varde-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Masthugg_Church" title="Masthugg Church">Masthugg Church</a> is a noted example of the style of this period.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> In the early 1920s, on the city\'s 300th anniversary, the <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6taplatsen" title="G\xc3\xb6taplatsen">G\xc3\xb6taplatsen</a> square with its <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">Neoclassical</a> look was built.<sup id="cite_ref-varde_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-varde-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After this, the predominant style in Gothenburg and rest of Sweden was <a href="/wiki/Functionalism_(architecture)" title="Functionalism (architecture)">Functionalism</a> which especially dominated the suburbs such as <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A4stra_Fr%C3%B6lunda" title="V\xc3\xa4stra Fr\xc3\xb6lunda">V\xc3\xa4stra Fr\xc3\xb6lunda</a> and Bergsj\xc3\xb6n. The Swedish functionalist architect <a href="/wiki/Uno_%C3%85hr%C3%A9n" title="Uno \xc3\x85hr\xc3\xa9n">Uno \xc3\x85hr\xc3\xa9n</a> served as city planner from 1932 through 1943.<sup id="cite_ref-varde_63-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-varde-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> In the 1950s, the big stadium <a href="/wiki/Ullevi" title="Ullevi">Ullevi</a> was built when Sweden hosted the <a href="/wiki/1958_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1958 FIFA World Cup">1958 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Summerburst_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Summerburst-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The modern architecture of the city has been formed by such architects as <a href="/wiki/Gert_Wing%C3%A5rdh" title="Gert Wing\xc3\xa5rdh">Gert Wing\xc3\xa5rdh</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> who started as a <a href="/wiki/Postmodernism" title="Postmodernism">Post-modernist</a> in the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Gustaf_Adolfs_torg,_Gothenburg" title="Gustaf Adolfs torg, Gothenburg">Gustaf Adolf Square</a> is a town square located in central Gothenburg. Noted buildings on the square include Gothenburg City Hall (formerly the stock exchange, opened in 1849) and the  <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Classicism" title="Nordic Classicism">Nordic Classicism</a> law court. The main canal of Gothenburg also flanks the square.<sup id="cite_ref-varde_63-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-varde-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Characteristic_buildings">Characteristic buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Characteristic buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barken_Viking_i_G%C3%B6teborg.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Barken_Viking_i_G%C3%B6teborg.JPG/220px-Barken_Viking_i_G%C3%B6teborg.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Barken_Viking_i_G%C3%B6teborg.JPG/330px-Barken_Viking_i_G%C3%B6teborg.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Barken_Viking_i_G%C3%B6teborg.JPG/440px-Barken_Viking_i_G%C3%B6teborg.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2564" data-file-height="1684" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barken_Viking_i_G%C3%B6teborg.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Skanskaskrapan</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_Central_Station" title="Gothenburg Central Station">Gothenburg Central Station</a> is in the centre of the city, next to Nordstan and Drottningtorget.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The building has been renovated and expanded numerous times since the grand opening in October 1858. In 2003, a major reconstruction was finished which brought the 19th-century building into the 21st century expanding the capacity for trains, travellers, and shopping.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Not far from the central station is the <a href="/wiki/Lilla_Bommen_(building)" title="Lilla Bommen (building)">Skanskaskrapan</a>, or more commonly known as "The Lipstick". It is 86&#160;m (282&#160;ft) high with 22&#160;floors and coloured in red-white stripes. The skyscraper was designed by <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Erskine_(architect)" title="Ralph Erskine (architect)">Ralph Erskine</a> and built by <a href="/wiki/Skanska" title="Skanska">Skanska</a> in the late 1980s as the headquarters for the company.<sup id="cite_ref-vasa_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vasa-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the shore of the G\xc3\xb6ta \xc3\x84lv at <a href="/wiki/Lilla_Bommen" title="Lilla Bommen">Lilla Bommen</a> is The G\xc3\xb6teborg Opera. It was completed in 1994. The architect Jan Izikowitz was inspired by the landscape and described his vision as "Something that makes your mind float over the squiggling landscape like the wings of a seagull."<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Feskek%C3%B6rka-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Feskek%C3%B6rka-1.jpg/220px-Feskek%C3%B6rka-1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Feskek%C3%B6rka-1.jpg/330px-Feskek%C3%B6rka-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Feskek%C3%B6rka-1.jpg/440px-Feskek%C3%B6rka-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2912" data-file-height="1875" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Feskek%C3%B6rka-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Feskek\xc3\xb6rka</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Feskek%C3%B6rka" class="mw-redirect" title="Feskek\xc3\xb6rka">Feskek\xc3\xb6rka</a>, or <i>Fiskhallen</i>, is an indoor fishmarket by the Rosenlundskanalen in central Gothenburg. Feskek\xc3\xb6rkan was opened on 1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>November 1874 and its name from the building\'s resemblance to a <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> church.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_city_hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Gothenburg city hall">Gothenburg city hall</a> is in the <a href="/wiki/Beaux-Arts_architecture" title="Beaux-Arts architecture">Beaux-Arts</a> architectural style. The <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_Synagogue" title="Gothenburg Synagogue">Gothenburg Synagogue</a> at Stora Nygatan, near Drottningtorget, was built in 1855 according to the designs of the German architect August Kr\xc3\xbcger.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Gunnebo_House" title="Gunnebo House">Gunnebo House</a> is a country house located to the south of Gothenburg, in M\xc3\xb6lndal. It was built in a neoclassical architecture towards the end of the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Created in the early 1900s was the <a href="/wiki/Vasa_Church,_Gothenburg" title="Vasa Church, Gothenburg">Vasa Church</a>. It is located in <a href="/wiki/Vasastan,_Gothenburg" title="Vasastan, Gothenburg">Vasastan</a> and is built of granite in a neo-Romanesque style.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another noted construction is <a href="/wiki/Brudaremossen_masts" title="Brudaremossen masts">Brudaremossen TV Tower</a>, one of the few <a href="/wiki/Partially_guyed_tower" title="Partially guyed tower">partially guyed towers</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Poseidon_statue.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Poseidon_statue.jpg/170px-Poseidon_statue.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Poseidon_statue.jpg/255px-Poseidon_statue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Poseidon_statue.jpg/340px-Poseidon_statue.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2872" data-file-height="3168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Poseidon_statue.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Poseidon Statue at G\xc3\xb6taplatsen, a well-known cultural symbol and landmark</div></div></div>\n<p>The sea, trade, and industrial history of the city are evident in the cultural life of Gothenburg. It is also a popular destination for tourists on the Swedish west coast.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Many of the cultural institutions, as well as hospitals and the university, were created by donations from rich merchants and industrialists, for example the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%B6hsska_Museum" title="R\xc3\xb6hsska Museum">R\xc3\xb6hsska Museum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> On 29<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>December 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_World_Culture" title="Museum of World Culture">Museum of World Culture</a> opened near <a href="/wiki/Korsv%C3%A4gen" title="Korsv\xc3\xa4gen">Korsv\xc3\xa4gen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sfv_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sfv-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Museums include the <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6teborgs_Konsthall" title="G\xc3\xb6teborgs Konsthall">Gothenburg Museum of Art</a>, and several museums of sea and navigation history, natural history, the sciences, and East India.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6ta_Air_Force_Wing" class="mw-redirect" title="G\xc3\xb6ta Air Force Wing">Aeroseum</a>, close to the G\xc3\xb6teborg City Airport, is an aircraft museum in a former military underground air force base.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Volvo_Museum" title="Volvo Museum">Volvo museum</a> has exhibits of the history of Volvo and the development from 1927 until today. Products shown include cars, trucks, marine engines, and buses.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Universeum" title="Universeum">Universeum</a> is a public science centre that opened in 2001, the largest of its kind in Scandinavia. It is divided into six sections, each containing experimental workshops and a collection of reptiles, fish, and insects.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Universeum occasionally host debates between Swedish secondary-school students and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates" title="List of Nobel laureates">Nobel Prize laureates</a> or other scholars.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leisure_and_entertainment">Leisure and entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Leisure and entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lisebergsentr%C3%A9n.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Lisebergsentr%C3%A9n.jpg/170px-Lisebergsentr%C3%A9n.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Lisebergsentr%C3%A9n.jpg/255px-Lisebergsentr%C3%A9n.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Lisebergsentr%C3%A9n.jpg/340px-Lisebergsentr%C3%A9n.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lisebergsentr%C3%A9n.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Liseberg amusement park</div></div></div>\n<p>The most noted attraction is the amusement park <a href="/wiki/Liseberg" title="Liseberg">Liseberg</a>, located in the central part of the city. It is the largest amusement park in Scandinavia by number of rides,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> and was chosen as one of the top ten amusement parks in the world (2005) by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> It is the most popular attraction in Sweden by number of visitors per year (more than 3&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-Adventure_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adventure-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are a number of independent theatre ensembles in the city, besides institutions such as <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_City_Theatre" title="Gothenburg City Theatre">Gothenburg City Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Backa_Theatre" title="Backa Theatre">Backa Theatre</a> (youth theatre), and <a href="/wiki/Folkteatern" title="Folkteatern">Folkteatern</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The main boulevard is called Kungsportsavenyn (commonly known as <i>Avenyn</i>, "The Avenue"). It is about 1&#160;km (0.6&#160;mi) long and starts at G\xc3\xb6taplatsen&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 which is the location of the <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_Museum_of_Art" title="Gothenburg Museum of Art">Gothenburg Museum of Art</a>, the city\'s theatre, and the city library, as well as the concert hall \xe2\x80\x93 and stretches all the way to <a href="/wiki/Kungsportsplatsen" title="Kungsportsplatsen">Kungsportsplatsen</a> in the old city centre of Gothenburg, crossing a canal and a small park.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Avenyn</i> was created in the 1860s and 1870s as a result of an international architecture contest, and is the product of a period of extensive town planning and remodelling.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> <i>Avenyn</i> has Gothenburg\'s highest concentration of pubs and clubs. Gothenburg\'s largest shopping centre (8th largest in Sweden), <a href="/wiki/Nordstan" title="Nordstan">Nordstan</a>, is located in central Gothenburg.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haganygata.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Haganygata.jpg/220px-Haganygata.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Haganygata.jpg/330px-Haganygata.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Haganygata.jpg/440px-Haganygata.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Haganygata.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Haga district</div></div></div>\n<p>Gothenburg\'s <a href="/wiki/Haga,_Gothenburg" title="Haga, Gothenburg">Haga</a> district is known for its picturesque wooden houses<sup id="cite_ref-Adventure_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adventure-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> and its caf\xc3\xa9s serving the well-known <i>Haga bulle</i> \xe2\x80\x93 a large cinnamon roll similar to the <i><a href="/wiki/Cinnamon_roll" title="Cinnamon roll">kanelbulle</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Five Gothenburg restaurants have a star in the 2008 <i><a href="/wiki/Michelin_Guide" title="Michelin Guide">Michelin Guide</a></i>: 28&#160;+, Basement, Fond, Kock &amp; Vin, Fiskekrogen, and Sj\xc3\xb6magasinet.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\nThe city has a number of star chefs&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 over the past decade, seven of the Swedish Chef of the Year awards have been won by people from Gothenburg.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Gustavus_Adolphus_pastry" title="Gustavus Adolphus pastry">Gustavus Adolphus pastry</a>, eaten every 6<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>November in Sweden, <a href="/wiki/Gustavus_Adolphus_Day" title="Gustavus Adolphus Day">Gustavus Adolphus Day</a>, is especially connected to, and appreciated in, Gothenburg because the city was founded by King Gustavus Adolphus.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>One of Gothenburg\'s most popular natural tourist attractions is the southern <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_archipelago" title="Gothenburg archipelago">Gothenburg archipelago</a>, which is a set of several islands that can be reached by ferry boats mainly operating from <a href="/wiki/Saltholmen_(Gothenburg)" class="mw-redirect" title="Saltholmen (Gothenburg)">Saltholmen</a>. Within the archipelago are the <a href="/wiki/%C3%84lvsborg_fortress" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc3\x84lvsborg fortress">\xc3\x84lvsborg fortress</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinga_(Gothenburg)" title="Vinga (Gothenburg)">Vinga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Styrs%C3%B6" title="Styrs\xc3\xb6">Styrs\xc3\xb6</a> islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Adventure_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adventure-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals_and_fairs">Festivals and fairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Festivals and fairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Goteborg_Gothia_Towers_4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Goteborg_Gothia_Towers_4.jpg/170px-Goteborg_Gothia_Towers_4.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Goteborg_Gothia_Towers_4.jpg/255px-Goteborg_Gothia_Towers_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Goteborg_Gothia_Towers_4.jpg/340px-Goteborg_Gothia_Towers_4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2112" data-file-height="2816" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Goteborg_Gothia_Towers_4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Discussion</i> by Nanna Ullman (1957) in front of the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Exhibition_and_Congress_Centre" title="Swedish Exhibition and Congress Centre">Swedish Exhibition and Congress Centre</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The annual <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_Film_Festival" title="Gothenburg Film Festival">Gothenburg Film Festival</a>, is the largest film festival in Scandinavia.<sup id="cite_ref-filmfestival_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-filmfestival-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_Book_Fair" title="Gothenburg Book Fair">Gothenburg Book Fair</a>, held each year in September.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> It is the largest literary festival in Scandinavia, and the second largest book fair in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-metro_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metro-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> A radical bookfair is held at the same time at the <a href="/wiki/Syndikalistiskt_Forum" title="Syndikalistiskt Forum">Syndikalistiskt Forum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Radikal_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Radikal-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Science_Festival_in_Gothenburg" title="International Science Festival in Gothenburg">International Science Festival in Gothenburg</a> is an annual festival since April 1997, in central Gothenburg with thought-provoking science activities for the public. The festival is visited by about <span class="nowrap">100,000</span> people each year.<sup id="cite_ref-vgforsok_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vgforsok-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> This makes it the largest popular-science event in Sweden<sup id="cite_ref-festhome_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-festhome-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> and one of the leading popular-science events in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Citing the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x9308">financial crisis</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Library_Associations_and_Institutions" title="International Federation of Library Associations and Institutions">International Federation of Library Associations and Institutions</a> moved the 2010 World Library and Information Congress, previously to be held in <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a>, Australia, to Gothenburg. The event took place on 10\xe2\x80\x9315<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>August 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_bands_from_Gothenburg" title="List of bands from Gothenburg">List of bands from Gothenburg</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Way_out_west-entrance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Way_out_west-entrance.jpg/220px-Way_out_west-entrance.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Way_out_west-entrance.jpg/330px-Way_out_west-entrance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Way_out_west-entrance.jpg/440px-Way_out_west-entrance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Way_out_west-entrance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Entrance to the Way Out West Festival</div></div></div>\n<p>Gothenburg has a diverse music community\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Gothenburg Symphony Orchestra">Gothenburg Symphony Orchestra</a> is the best-known in classical music.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Gothenburg also was the birthplace of the Swedish composer <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Atterberg" title="Kurt Atterberg">Kurt Atterberg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> The first internationally successfully Swedish group, <a href="/wiki/Instrumental_rock" title="Instrumental rock">instrumental rock</a> group <a href="/wiki/The_Spotnicks" title="The Spotnicks">The Spotnicks</a> came from Gothenburg.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>Bands such as <a href="/wiki/The_Soundtrack_of_Our_Lives" title="The Soundtrack of Our Lives">The Soundtrack of Our Lives</a><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ace_of_Base" title="Ace of Base">Ace of Base</a> are well-known pop representatives of the city. During the 1970s, Gothenburg had strong roots in the Swedish progressive movement (<a href="/wiki/Progg" title="Progg">progg</a>) with such groups as <a href="/wiki/Nationalteatern" title="Nationalteatern">Nationalteatern</a>, Nynningen, and Motvind. The record company Nacksving and the editorial office for the magazine Musikens Makt which also were part of the progg movement was located in Gothenburg during this time as well.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>There is also an active indie scene in Gothenburg. For example, the musician <a href="/wiki/Jens_Lekman" title="Jens Lekman">Jens Lekman</a> was born in the suburb of Angered<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> and named his 2007 release <i><a href="/wiki/Night_Falls_Over_Kortedala" title="Night Falls Over Kortedala">Night Falls Over Kortedala</a></i> after another suburb, <a href="/wiki/Kortedala" title="Kortedala">Kortedala</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Other internationally acclaimed indie artists include the electro pop duos <a href="/wiki/Studio_(band)" title="Studio (band)">Studio</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Knife" title="The Knife">The Knife</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Air_France_(band)" title="Air France (band)">Air France</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Tough_Alliance" title="The Tough Alliance">The Tough Alliance</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> indie rock band <a href="/wiki/Love_Is_All_(band)" title="Love Is All (band)">Love is All</a>, songwriter <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Gonz%C3%A1lez_(singer)" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Gonz\xc3\xa1lez (singer)">Jos\xc3\xa9 Gonz\xc3\xa1lez</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> and pop singer <a href="/wiki/El_Perro_del_Mar" title="El Perro del Mar">El Perro del Mar</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> as well as genre-bending quartet <a href="/wiki/Little_Dragon" title="Little Dragon">Little Dragon</a> fronted by vocalist <a href="/wiki/Yukimi_Nagano" title="Yukimi Nagano">Yukimi Nagano</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Another son of the city is one of Sweden\'s most popular singers, <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A5kan_Hellstr%C3%B6m" title="H\xc3\xa5kan Hellstr\xc3\xb6m">H\xc3\xa5kan Hellstr\xc3\xb6m</a>, who often includes many places from the city in his songs.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Glam_rock" title="Glam rock">glam rock</a> group <a href="/wiki/Supergroupies" title="Supergroupies">Supergroupies</a> derives from Gothenburg.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gothenburg\'s own commercially successful <a href="/wiki/At_the_Gates" title="At the Gates">At the Gates</a>, <a href="/wiki/In_Flames" title="In Flames">In Flames</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dark_Tranquillity" title="Dark Tranquillity">Dark Tranquillity</a> are credited with pioneering <a href="/wiki/Melodic_death_metal" title="Melodic death metal">melodic death metal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Other well-known bands of the Gothenburg scene are thrash metal band <a href="/wiki/The_Haunted_(Swedish_band)" title="The Haunted (Swedish band)">The Haunted</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> progressive power metal band <a href="/wiki/Evergrey" title="Evergrey">Evergrey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> and power metal bands <a href="/wiki/HammerFall" title="HammerFall">HammerFall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dream_Evil" title="Dream Evil">Dream Evil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Many music festivals take place in the city every year. The <a href="/wiki/Metaltown_Festival" title="Metaltown Festival">Metaltown Festival</a> is a two-day festival featuring <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal music</a> bands, held in Gothenburg. It has been arranged annually since 2004, taking place at the Frihamnen venue.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> In June 2012, the festival included bands such as In Flames, <a href="/wiki/Marilyn_Manson" title="Marilyn Manson">Marilyn Manson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slayer" title="Slayer">Slayer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lamb_of_God_(band)" title="Lamb of God (band)">Lamb of God</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mastodon_(band)" title="Mastodon (band)">Mastodon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Another popular festival, Way Out West, focuses more on <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip-hop</a> genres.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fyrverkeri_p%C3%A5_Gothia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Fyrverkeri_p%C3%A5_Gothia.jpg/220px-Fyrverkeri_p%C3%A5_Gothia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Fyrverkeri_p%C3%A5_Gothia.jpg/330px-Fyrverkeri_p%C3%A5_Gothia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Fyrverkeri_p%C3%A5_Gothia.jpg/440px-Fyrverkeri_p%C3%A5_Gothia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4028" data-file-height="2680" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fyrverkeri_p%C3%A5_Gothia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fireworks at the opening ceremony of Gothia Cup</div></div></div>\n<p>As in all of Sweden, a variety of sports are followed, including <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Handball" title="Handball">handball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Floorball" title="Floorball">floorball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pes%C3%A4pallo" title="Pes\xc3\xa4pallo">baseball</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Figure_skating" title="Figure skating">figure skating</a>. A varied amateur and professional sports clubs scene exists.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gothenburg is the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Sweden" title="Football in Sweden">football in Sweden</a> as the <a href="/wiki/First_football_match_in_Sweden" title="First football match in Sweden">first football match in Sweden</a> was played there in 1892.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The city\'s three major football clubs, <a href="/wiki/IFK_G%C3%B6teborg" title="IFK G\xc3\xb6teborg">IFK G\xc3\xb6teborg</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%96rgryte_IS" title="\xc3\x96rgryte IS">\xc3\x96rgryte IS</a>, and <a href="/wiki/GAIS" title="GAIS">GAIS</a><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> share a total of 34 Swedish championships between them.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> IFK has also won the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a> twice.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Other notable clubs include <a href="/wiki/BK_H%C3%A4cken" title="BK H\xc3\xa4cken">BK H\xc3\xa4cken</a> (football),<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6teborg_HC" title="G\xc3\xb6teborg HC">G\xc3\xb6teborg HC</a> (women\'s ice hockey), <a href="/wiki/Pixbo_Wallenstam_IBK" title="Pixbo Wallenstam IBK">Pixbo Wallenstam IBK</a> (<a href="/wiki/Floorball" title="Floorball">floorball</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> multiple national handball champion <a href="/wiki/Redbergslids_IK" title="Redbergslids IK">Redbergslids IK</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> and four-time national ice hockey champion <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%B6lunda_HC" title="Fr\xc3\xb6lunda HC">Fr\xc3\xb6lunda HC</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Gothenburg had a professional basketball team, <a href="/wiki/Gothia_Basket" title="Gothia Basket">Gothia Basket</a>, until 2010 when it ceased.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bandy" title="Bandy">bandy</a> department of GAIS, <a href="/wiki/GAIS_Bandy" title="GAIS Bandy">GAIS Bandy</a>, played the first season in the highest division <a href="/wiki/Elitserien_(bandy)" title="Elitserien (bandy)">Elitserien</a> last season. The group stage match between the main rivals <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_bandy_team" title="Sweden national bandy team">Sweden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russia_national_bandy_team" title="Russia national bandy team">Russia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2013_Bandy_World_Championship" title="2013 Bandy World Championship">2013 Bandy World Championship</a> was played at <a href="/wiki/Heden" title="Heden">Arena Heden</a> in central Gothenburg.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city\'s most notable sports venues are <a href="/wiki/Scandinavium" title="Scandinavium">Scandinavium</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> and Ullevi (multisport) and the newly built <a href="/wiki/Gamla_Ullevi" title="Gamla Ullevi">Gamla Ullevi</a><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> (football).\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2003_World_Allround_Speed_Skating_Championships" title="2003 World Allround Speed Skating Championships">2003 World Allround Speed Skating Championships</a> were held in Rudhallen, <a href="/wiki/List_of_indoor_speed_skating_rinks" title="List of indoor speed skating rinks">Sweden\'s only indoor speed-skating arena</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> It is a part of Ruddalens&#160;IP, which also has a bandy field and several football fields.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The only Swedish heavyweight champion of the world in boxing, <a href="/wiki/Ingemar_Johansson" title="Ingemar Johansson">Ingemar Johansson</a>, who took the title from Floyd Paterson in 1959, was from Gothenburg.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:B%C3%A5tar_vid_Saltholmen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/B%C3%A5tar_vid_Saltholmen.jpg/220px-B%C3%A5tar_vid_Saltholmen.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/B%C3%A5tar_vid_Saltholmen.jpg/330px-B%C3%A5tar_vid_Saltholmen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/B%C3%A5tar_vid_Saltholmen.jpg/440px-B%C3%A5tar_vid_Saltholmen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="1696" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:B%C3%A5tar_vid_Saltholmen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Boats at Saltholmen in the Gothenburg archipelago</div></div></div>\n<p>Gothenburg has hosted a number of international sporting events including the <a href="/wiki/1958_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1958 FIFA World Cup">1958 FIFA World Cup</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Summerburst_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Summerburst-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/1983_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup_Final" title="1983 European Cup Winners&#39; Cup Final">1983 European Cup Winners\' Cup Final</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> an <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a> preseason game on 14<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>August 1988 between the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bears" title="Chicago Bears">Chicago Bears</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Vikings" title="Minnesota Vikings">Minnesota Vikings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/1992_European_Football_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="1992 European Football Championship">1992 European Football Championship</a>, the 1993<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> and the 2002 <a href="/wiki/World_Men%27s_Handball_Championship" title="World Men&#39;s Handball Championship">World Men\'s Handball Championship</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-got_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-got-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/1995_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1995 World Championships in Athletics">1995 World Championships in Athletics</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> the 1997 World Championships in Swimming (short track),<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> the 2002 <a href="/wiki/Ice_Hockey_World_Championships" title="Ice Hockey World Championships">Ice Hockey World Championships</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-got_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-got-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> the 2004 UEFA Cup final,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/2006_European_Championships_in_Athletics" class="mw-redirect" title="2006 European Championships in Athletics">2006 European Championships in Athletics</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/2008_World_Figure_Skating_Championships" title="2008 World Figure Skating Championships">2008 World Figure Skating Championships</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> Annual events held in the city are the <a href="/wiki/Gothia_Cup" title="Gothia Cup">Gothia Cup</a><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6teborgsvarvet" title="G\xc3\xb6teborgsvarvet">G\xc3\xb6teborgsvarvet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vastra_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vastra-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>  The annual <a href="/wiki/Gothia_Cup" title="Gothia Cup">Gothia Cup</a>, is the world\'s largest football tournament with regards to the number of participants: in 2011, a total of 35,200 players from 1,567 teams and 72 nations participated.\n</p><p>Gothenburg hosted the XIII&#160;<a href="/wiki/FINA_World_Masters_Championships" title="FINA World Masters Championships">FINA World Masters Championships</a> in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Diving, swimming, synchronized swimming and open-water competitions were held on 28<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>July to 7<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>August. The water polo events were played on the neighboring city of <a href="/wiki/Bor%C3%A5s" title="Bor\xc3\xa5s">Bor\xc3\xa5s</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gothenburg is also home to the Gothenburg Sharks, a professional baseball team in the <a href="/wiki/Elitserien_(baseball)" title="Elitserien (baseball)">Elitserien</a> division of baseball in Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With around 25,000 sailboats and yachts scattered about the city, sailing is a popular sports activity in the region, particularly because of the nearby Gothenburg archipelago.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> In June 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Volvo_Ocean_Race" class="mw-redirect" title="Volvo Ocean Race">Volvo Ocean Race</a>, professional sailing\'s leading crewed offshore race, concluded in Gothenburg,<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> as well as an event in the 2015\xe2\x80\x932016 <a href="/wiki/America%27s_Cup_World_Series" title="America&#39;s Cup World Series">America\'s Cup World Series</a> in August 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Gadk" title="Gadk">Gothenburg Amateur Diving Club</a> (G\xc3\xb6teborgs amat\xc3\xb6rdykarklubb) Has been operating since October 1938.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wingquist_bearing00.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Wingquist_bearing00.jpg/170px-Wingquist_bearing00.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Wingquist_bearing00.jpg/255px-Wingquist_bearing00.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Wingquist_bearing00.jpg/340px-Wingquist_bearing00.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1652" data-file-height="1697" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wingquist_bearing00.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>SKF Wingquist self-aligning bearing</div></div></div>\n<p>Due to Gothenburg\'s advantageous location in the centre of Scandinavia, trade and shipping have always played a major role in the city\'s economic history, and they continue to do so. Gothenburg port has come to be the largest harbour in <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-selimw_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-selimw-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Apart from trade, the second pillar of Gothenburg has traditionally been manufacturing and industry, which significantly contributes to the city\'s wealth.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Major companies operating plants in the area include SKF, Volvo (both cars and trucks), and <a href="/wiki/Ericsson" title="Ericsson">Ericsson</a>. <a href="/wiki/Volvo_Cars" title="Volvo Cars">Volvo Cars</a> is the largest employer in Gothenburg, not including jobs in supply companies. The blue-collar industries which have dominated the city for long are still important factors in the city\'s economy, but they are being gradually replaced by high-tech industries.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Banking and finance are also important, as well as the event and tourist industry.<sup id="cite_ref-selimw_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-selimw-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gothenburg is the terminus of the Valdemar-G\xc3\xb6teborg gas <a href="/wiki/Pipeline_transport" title="Pipeline transport">pipeline</a>, which brings natural gas from the North Sea fields to Sweden, through Denmark.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Historically, Gothenburg was home base from the 18th century of the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_East_India_Company" title="Swedish East India Company">Swedish East India Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> From its founding until the late 1970s, the city was a world leader in shipbuilding, with such shipyards as <a href="/wiki/Eriksbergs_Mekaniska_Verkstad" title="Eriksbergs Mekaniska Verkstad">Eriksbergs Mekaniska Verkstad</a>, G\xc3\xb6taverken, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Arendalsvarvet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Arendalsvarvet (page does not exist)">Arendalsvarvet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lindholmens_varv" class="mw-redirect" title="Lindholmens varv">Lindholmens varv</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Gothenburg is classified as a <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a> by <a href="/wiki/GaWC" class="mw-redirect" title="GaWC">GaWC</a>, with a ranking of Gamma.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> The city has been ranked as the 12th-most inventive city in the world by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_Municipality" title="Gothenburg Municipality">Gothenburg Municipality</a></div>\n<p>Gothenburg became a city municipality with an elected city council when the first Swedish local government acts were implemented in 1863.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The municipality has an assembly consisting of 81 members,<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> elected every fourth year.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Political decisions depend on citizens considering them legitimate. Political legitimacy can be based on various factors: legality, due process, and equality before the law, as well as the efficiency and effectiveness of public policy. One method used to achieve greater legitimacy for controversial policy reforms such as congestion charges is to allow citizens to decide or advise on the issue in public referendums. In December 2010 a petition for a local referendum on the congestion tax, signed by 28,000 citizens, was submitted to the City Council. This right to submit so-called \xe2\x80\x9cpeople\'s initiatives\xe2\x80\x9d was inscribed in the Local Government Act, which obliged local governments to hold a local referendum if petitioned by 5% of the citizens unless the issue was deemed to be outside their area of jurisdiction or if a majority in the City Council voted against holding such a referendum.<sup id="cite_ref-Hysing_1\xe2\x80\x938_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hysing_1\xe2\x80\x938-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> A second petition for a referendum, signed by 57,000 citizens, was submitted to the local government in February 2013. This petition followed a campaign organised by a local newspaper \xe2\x80\x93 G\xc3\xb6teborgs Tidningen \xe2\x80\x93 whose editor-in-chief argued that the paper\'s involvement was justified by the large public response to a series of articles on the congestion tax, as well as out of concern for the local democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hysing_1\xe2\x80\x938_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hysing_1\xe2\x80\x938-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1008px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:G2Atorg-panorama.jpg" class="image" title="View over Gustav Adolfs torg, square named after Gustavus Adolphus, the founding father of Gothenburg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/G2Atorg-panorama.jpg/1000px-G2Atorg-panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="1000" height="162" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/G2Atorg-panorama.jpg/1500px-G2Atorg-panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/G2Atorg-panorama.jpg/2000px-G2Atorg-panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8736" data-file-height="1416" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:G2Atorg-panorama.jpg" title="File:G2Atorg-panorama.jpg"> </a></div>View over <a href="/wiki/Gustaf_Adolfs_torg,_G%C3%B6teborg" class="mw-redirect" title="Gustaf Adolfs torg, G\xc3\xb6teborg">Gustav Adolfs torg</a>, square named after <a href="/wiki/Gustavus_Adolphus" class="mw-redirect" title="Gustavus Adolphus">Gustavus Adolphus</a>, the founding father of Gothenburg</div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Proportion_of_foreign_born">Proportion of foreign born</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
