title="Germany">Germany</a></td>\n<td>2,832\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>In 2019, approximately 28% (159,342 residents) of the population of Gothenburg were foreign born and approximately 46% (265,019 residents) had at least one parent born abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> In addition, approximately 12% (69,263 residents) were foreign citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2016, 45% of Gothenburg\'s immigrant population is from other parts of Europe, and 10% of the total population is from another Nordic country.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_177-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Gothenburg has two universities, both of which started as colleges founded by private donations in the 19th century. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Gothenburg" title="University of Gothenburg">University of Gothenburg</a> has about 38,000 students and is one of the largest universities in Scandinavia,<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> and one of the most versatile in Sweden. <a href="/wiki/Chalmers_University_of_Technology" title="Chalmers University of Technology">Chalmers University of Technology</a> is a well-known university located in Johanneberg 2&#160;km (1&#160;mi) south of the inner city, lately also established at Lindholmen in Norra \xc3\x84lvstranden, Hisingen.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2015, there were ten <a href="/wiki/Folk_high_school" title="Folk high school">adult education centres</a> in Gothenburg: <i>Agnesbergs folkh\xc3\xb6gskola</i>, <i>Arbetarr\xc3\xb6relsens folkh\xc3\xb6gskola i G\xc3\xb6teborg</i>, <i>Finska folkh\xc3\xb6gskolan</i>, <i>Folkh\xc3\xb6gskolan i Angered</i>, <i>G\xc3\xb6teborgs folkh\xc3\xb6gskola</i>, <i>Kvinnofolkh\xc3\xb6gskolan</i>, <i>Mo G\xc3\xa5rd folkh\xc3\xb6gskola</i>, <i>S:ta Birgittas folkh\xc3\xb6gskola</i>, <i>V\xc3\xa4stra G\xc3\xb6talands folkh\xc3\xb6gskolor</i> and <i>Wendelsbergs folkh\xc3\xb6gskola</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2015, there were 49 <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">high schools</a> Gothenburg. Some of the more notable schools are <a href="/wiki/Hvitfeldtska_gymnasiet" title="Hvitfeldtska gymnasiet">Hvitfeldtska gymnasiet</a>, <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6teborgs_H%C3%B6gre_Samskola" title="G\xc3\xb6teborgs H\xc3\xb6gre Samskola">G\xc3\xb6teborgs H\xc3\xb6gre Samskola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigrid_Rudebecks_gymnasium" class="mw-redirect" title="Sigrid Rudebecks gymnasium">Sigrid Rudebecks gymnasium</a> and Polhemsgymnasiet. Some high-schools are also connected to large Swedish corporations, such as SKF Technical high-school that is owned by <a href="/wiki/SKF" title="SKF">SKF</a> and Gothenburg\'s technical high-school that is jointly owned by <a href="/wiki/Volvo_AB" class="mw-redirect" title="Volvo AB">Volvo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volvo_Cars" title="Volvo Cars">Volvo Cars</a> and Gothenburg municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are two folkh\xc3\xb6gskola that teach fine arts: Domen and Goteborg Folkh\xc3\xb6gskola.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tram_2_at_Brunnsparken.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Tram_2_at_Brunnsparken.jpg/220px-Tram_2_at_Brunnsparken.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Tram_2_at_Brunnsparken.jpg/330px-Tram_2_at_Brunnsparken.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Tram_2_at_Brunnsparken.jpg/440px-Tram_2_at_Brunnsparken.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="2136" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tram_2_at_Brunnsparken.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gothenburg\'s trams</div></div></div>\n<p>With over 90&#160;km (56&#160;mi) of double track, the <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_tram_network" title="Gothenburg tram network">Gothenburg tram network</a> covers most of the city and is the largest <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">tram</a>/<a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> network in Scandinavia. Gothenburg also has a bus network. Boat and <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferry</a> services connect the <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_archipelago" title="Gothenburg archipelago">Gothenburg archipelago</a> to the mainland. The lack of a <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">subway</a> is due to the soft ground on which Gothenburg is situated. Tunneling is very expensive in such conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\nThe Gothenburg <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_commuter_rail" title="Gothenburg commuter rail">commuter rail</a> with three lines services some nearby cities and towns.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_and_intercity_bus">Rail and intercity bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Rail and intercity bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Platforms_at_Gothenburg_central_bus_station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Platforms_at_Gothenburg_central_bus_station.jpg/220px-Platforms_at_Gothenburg_central_bus_station.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Platforms_at_Gothenburg_central_bus_station.jpg/330px-Platforms_at_Gothenburg_central_bus_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Platforms_at_Gothenburg_central_bus_station.jpg/440px-Platforms_at_Gothenburg_central_bus_station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Platforms_at_Gothenburg_central_bus_station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Platforms at Gothenburg bus station.</div></div></div>\n<p>Other major transportation hubs are <i>Centralstationen</i> (Gothenburg Central Station) and the <a href="/wiki/Nils_Ericson_Terminal" title="Nils Ericson Terminal">Nils Ericson Terminal</a> with trains and buses to various destinations in Sweden, as well as connections to Oslo and Copenhagen (via <a href="/wiki/Malm%C3%B6" title="Malm\xc3\xb6">Malm\xc3\xb6</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r997900035"/><div class="locmap noviewer thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px"><div style="position:relative;width:220px;border:1px solid lightgray"><a href="/wiki/File:Sweden_V%C3%A4stra_G%C3%B6taland_location_map.svg" class="image" title="Gothenburg is located in V\xc3\xa4stra G\xc3\xb6taland"><img alt="Gothenburg is located in V\xc3\xa4stra G\xc3\xb6taland" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Sweden_V%C3%A4stra_G%C3%B6taland_location_map.svg/220px-Sweden_V%C3%A4stra_G%C3%B6taland_location_map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="234" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Sweden_V%C3%A4stra_G%C3%B6taland_location_map.svg/330px-Sweden_V%C3%A4stra_G%C3%B6taland_location_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Sweden_V%C3%A4stra_G%C3%B6taland_location_map.svg/440px-Sweden_V%C3%A4stra_G%C3%B6taland_location_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="940" data-file-height="1000" /></a><div class="od" style="top:75%;left:24.806%"><div class="id" style="left:-4px;top:-4px"><img alt="Gothenburg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/8px-Red_pog.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Gothenburg" width="8" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/12px-Red_pog.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/16px-Red_pog.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div></div><div class="od" style="top:76.667%;left:32.351%"><div class="id" style="left:-4px;top:-4px"><img alt="GOT" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Airplane_silhouette.svg/8px-Airplane_silhouette.svg.png" decoding="async" title="GOT" width="8" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Airplane_silhouette.svg/12px-Airplane_silhouette.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Airplane_silhouette.svg/16px-Airplane_silhouette.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="400" /></div><div class="pv" style="font-size:91%;width:6em;top:5px;left:-3em"><div><b><a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6teborg_Landvetter_Airport" title="G\xc3\xb6teborg Landvetter Airport">GOT</a></b></div></div></div><div class="od" style="top:71.852%;left:22.571%"><div class="id" style="left:-4px;top:-4px"><img alt="GSE" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Airplane_silhouette.svg/8px-Airplane_silhouette.svg.png" decoding="async" title="GSE" width="8" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Airplane_silhouette.svg/12px-Airplane_silhouette.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Airplane_silhouette.svg/16px-Airplane_silhouette.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="400" /></div><div class="pl" style="font-size:91%;width:6em;right:5px"><div><b><a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6teborg_City_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="G\xc3\xb6teborg City Airport">GSE</a></b></div></div></div></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sweden_V%C3%A4stra_G%C3%B6taland_location_map.svg" title="File:Sweden V\xc3\xa4stra G\xc3\xb6taland location map.svg"> </a></div>Map showing the locations of airports around Gothenburg</div></div></div>\n<p>Gothenburg is served by <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6teborg_Landvetter_Airport" title="G\xc3\xb6teborg Landvetter Airport">G\xc3\xb6teborg Landvetter Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>GOT</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>ESGG</b>), located about 20&#160;km (12&#160;mi) east of the city centre. It is named after nearby locality <a href="/wiki/Landvetter" title="Landvetter">Landvetter</a>. <a href="/wiki/Flygbussarna" title="Flygbussarna">Flygbussarna</a> offer frequent bus connections to and from Gothenburg with travel time 20\xe2\x80\x9330 minutes. <a href="/wiki/Swebus_Express" title="Swebus Express">Swebus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flixbus" title="Flixbus">Flixbus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nettbuss" class="mw-redirect" title="Nettbuss">Nettbuss</a> also serve the airport with several daily departures to Gothenburg, <a href="/wiki/Bor%C3%A5s" title="Bor\xc3\xa5s">Bor\xc3\xa5s</a> and other destinations along <a href="/wiki/European_route_E4" title="European route E4">European route E4</a>. <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A4sttrafik" title="V\xc3\xa4sttrafik">V\xc3\xa4sttrafik</a>, the local public transport provider in the area, offers additional connections to <a href="/wiki/Landvetter" title="Landvetter">Landvetter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airport is operated by Swedish national airport operator <a href="/wiki/Swedavia" title="Swedavia">Swedavia</a>, and with 6.8 million passengers served in 2017, it is Sweden\'s second-largest airport after <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport" title="Stockholm Arlanda Airport">Stockholm Arlanda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> It serves as a base for several domestic and international airlines, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_Shuttle" title="Norwegian Air Shuttle">Norwegian Air Shuttle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>. G\xc3\xb6teborg Landvetter, however, does not serve as a hub for any airline. In total, there are about 50 destinations with scheduled direct flights to and from Gothenburg, most of them European. An additional 40 destinations are served via charter.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The second airport in the area, <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6teborg_City_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="G\xc3\xb6teborg City Airport">G\xc3\xb6teborg City Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>GSE</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>ESGP</b>), is closed. On 13<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>January 2015, Swedish airport operator <a href="/wiki/Swedavia" title="Swedavia">Swedavia</a> announced that G\xc3\xb6teborg City Airport will not reopen for commercial services following an extensive rebuild of the airport started in November 2014, citing that the cost of making the airport viable for commercial operations again was too high, at 250 million kronor ($31 million). Commercial operations will be gradually wound down.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> The airport was located 10&#160;km (6&#160;mi) northwest of the city centre. It was formerly known as <i>S\xc3\xa4ve Flygplats.</i> It is located within the borders of <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg_Municipality" title="Gothenburg Municipality">Gothenburg Municipality</a>. In addition to commercial airlines, the airport was also operated by a number of rescue services, including the Swedish Coast Guard, and was used for other <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> Most civil air traffic to G\xc3\xb6teborg City Airport was via <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost airlines</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a>. Those companies have now been relocated to Landvetter Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sea">Sea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gothenburg,_Sweden,_from_the_%C3%84lsborgs_Bridge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Gothenburg%2C_Sweden%2C_from_the_%C3%84lsborgs_Bridge.jpg/220px-Gothenburg%2C_Sweden%2C_from_the_%C3%84lsborgs_Bridge.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Gothenburg%2C_Sweden%2C_from_the_%C3%84lsborgs_Bridge.jpg/330px-Gothenburg%2C_Sweden%2C_from_the_%C3%84lsborgs_Bridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Gothenburg%2C_Sweden%2C_from_the_%C3%84lsborgs_Bridge.jpg/440px-Gothenburg%2C_Sweden%2C_from_the_%C3%84lsborgs_Bridge.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1278" data-file-height="630" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gothenburg,_Sweden,_from_the_%C3%84lsborgs_Bridge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gothenburg harbour seen from the \xc3\x84lvsborg bridge, seen to the left is the ship <a href="/wiki/High-speed_Sea_Service" title="High-speed Sea Service">HSS <i>Stena Carisma</i></a> and to the right <a href="/wiki/MS_Stena_Scandinavica_(1983)" class="mw-redirect" title="MS Stena Scandinavica (1983)">MS <i>Stena Scandinavica</i> (1983)</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Swedish company <a href="/wiki/Stena_Line" title="Stena Line">Stena Line</a> operates between Gothenburg/<a href="/wiki/Frederikshavn" title="Frederikshavn">Frederikshavn</a> in Denmark and Gothenburg/<a href="/wiki/Kiel" title="Kiel">Kiel</a> in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The "England ferry" (<i>Englandsf\xc3\xa4rjan</i>) to Newcastle via <a href="/wiki/Kristiansand" title="Kristiansand">Kristiansand</a> (run by the Danish company <a href="/wiki/DFDS" title="DFDS">DFDS Seaways</a>) ceased at the end of October 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> after being a Gothenburg institution since the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> DFDS Seaways\' sister company, DFDS Tor Line, continues to run scheduled <a href="/wiki/Cargo" title="Cargo">cargo</a> ships between Gothenburg and several English ports, and these used to have limited capacity for passengers and their private vehicles. Also freight ships to North America and East Asia leave from the port.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Freight">Freight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Freight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Gothenburg is an intermodal logistics hub and Gothenburg harbour has access to Sweden and Norway via rail and trucks. Gothenburg harbour is the largest port in Scandinavia with a cargo turnover of 36.9&#160;million tonnes per year in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_connected_to_Gothenburg" class="mw-redirect" title="List of people connected to Gothenburg">List of people connected to Gothenburg</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Staty_Kal_ada_Lisebergs_entr%C3%A9.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Staty_Kal_ada_Lisebergs_entr%C3%A9.jpg/170px-Staty_Kal_ada_Lisebergs_entr%C3%A9.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Staty_Kal_ada_Lisebergs_entr%C3%A9.jpg/255px-Staty_Kal_ada_Lisebergs_entr%C3%A9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Staty_Kal_ada_Lisebergs_entr%C3%A9.jpg/340px-Staty_Kal_ada_Lisebergs_entr%C3%A9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="372" data-file-height="491" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Staty_Kal_ada_Lisebergs_entr%C3%A9.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kal and Ada at Liseberg</div></div></div>\n<p>Two of the noted people from Gothenburg are fictional, but have become synonymous with "people from Gothenburg". They are a working class couple called Kal and Ada, featured in "Gothenburg jokes" (<i>g\xc3\xb6teborgsvitsar</i>), songs, plays and names of events.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> Each year two persons who have significantly contributed to culture in the city are given the honorary titles of "Kal and Ada".<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> A bronze statue of the couple made by Svenrobert Lundquist, was placed outside the entrance to Liseberg in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Some of the noted people from Gothenburg are Academy Award Winning actress <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Vikander" title="Alicia Vikander">Alicia Vikander</a>, cookbook author <a href="/wiki/Sofia_von_Porat" title="Sofia von Porat">Sofia von Porat</a>, footballer <a href="/wiki/Gunnar_Gren" title="Gunnar Gren">Gunnar Gren</a>, artist <a href="/wiki/Evert_Taube" title="Evert Taube">Evert Taube</a>, golfer <a href="/wiki/Helen_Alfredsson" title="Helen Alfredsson">Helen Alfredsson</a>, industrialist <a href="/wiki/Victor_Hasselblad" title="Victor Hasselblad">Victor Hasselblad</a>, singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B6rn_Ulvaeus" title="Bj\xc3\xb6rn Ulvaeus">Bj\xc3\xb6rn Ulvaeus</a>, diplomat <a href="/wiki/Jan_Eliasson" title="Jan Eliasson">Jan Eliasson</a>, British Open Winner and professional golfer <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Stenson" title="Henrik Stenson">Henrik Stenson</a>, YouTuber <a href="/wiki/PewDiePie" title="PewDiePie">PewDiePie</a> (<a href="/wiki/PewDiePie" title="PewDiePie">Felix Kjellberg</a>), the most subscribed-to individual on the platform, with over 100 million subscribers <sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> and YouTuber <a href="/wiki/Joel_Berghult" title="Joel Berghult">RoomieOfficial</a> (<a href="/wiki/Joel_Berghult" title="Joel Berghult">Joel Berghult</a>).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_rankings">International rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: International rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Gothenburg has performed well in international rankings, some of which are mentioned below:\nThe Global Destination Sustainability Index has named Gothenburg the world\'s most sustainable destination every year since 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2019 Gothenburg was selected by the EU as one of the top 2020 European Capitals of Smart Tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2020 Business Region G\xc3\xb6teborg received the \'European Entrepreneurial Region Award 2020\' (EER Award 2020) from the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Gothenburg Award is the city\'s international prize that recognises and supports work to achieve sustainable development \xe2\x80\x93 in the Gothenburg region and from a global perspective.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> The award, which is one million Swedish crowns, is administrated and funded by a coalition of the City of Gothenburg and 12 companies.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>  Past winners of the award have included <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>, and Michael Biddle.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Sweden" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Sweden">List of twin towns and sister cities in Sweden</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gothenburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Twin towns and sister href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>\nGothenburg had signed an agreement with <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> in 1986 which was upgraded in 2003 to include exchanges in culture, economics, trade and sport. The agreement was allowed to lapse in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-hongkongfp_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hongkongfp-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline"
